# Edit or duplicate a container | Portainer Documentation

Editing a container effectively creates a new container with the updated settings and replaces the old container.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/edit#editing-a-running-container)

Editing a running container


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

From the menu select **Containers**, select the container you want to edit then click **Duplicate/Edit**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FqIMcLFfteYzLp0o52Gv8%2F2.15-docker_containers_container_edit.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=7792e7b6&sv=2)

Make the required changes to the container configuration. When you're finished, click **Deploy the container**. When the confirmation message appears, click **Replace**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FbCMJmXKxKVtsTQ1R7BnJ%2F2.15-container-edit-confirm.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=50ef6dfe&sv=2)

If successful, a message will appear confirming that a new container has been created with the new settings, replacing the old container.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/edit#duplicating-a-running-container)

Duplicating a running container


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

From the menu select **Containers**, select the container you want to duplicate then click **Duplicate/Edit**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FqIMcLFfteYzLp0o52Gv8%2F2.15-docker_containers_container_edit.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=7792e7b6&sv=2)

Make the required changes to the container configuration, making sure you enter a new container name in order to create a duplicate. When you're finished, click **Deploy the container**.

[PreviousInspect a container](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/inspect)
[NextAdvanced container settings](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/advanced)

Was this helpful?

---

# Advanced container settings | Portainer Documentation

When creating or editing a container you can configure a number of additional settings in the **Advanced container settings** section.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FZmHQXg3cAmHyPTd4I5wm%2F2.15-containers-advanced.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=297efcbb&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/advanced#command-and-logging)

Command & logging


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

In this section you can configure the command that runs when the container starts as well as configure logging for the container.

Field/Option

Overview

Command

Set the command that is run when the container starts. Select `Default` to use the default command provided by the container's image, or select `Override` and provide a command to override the default value.

Entrypoint

Set the entrypoint for the container. Select `Default` to use the default entrypoint provided by the container's image, or select `Override` and provide an entrypoint to override the default value.

Working Dir

Set the working directory your container should start in (within the container's filesystem).

User

Specify the user that the container's command should run as.

Console

Set the console configuration for your container.

Driver

Select the logging driver to use for your container. Available options will depend on the logging drivers configured on your Docker host.

Options

Set additional options for your logging driver. To add a new option click **add logging driver option** and configure accordingly.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FQTuxe0UMEyJ7JyJ06TD6%2F2.15-containers-advanced-command.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=c197414c&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/advanced#volumes)

Volumes


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Here you can configure volume mappings for your container. You can map to [existing named volumes](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/volumes)
 or bind mount to locations on your Docker host.

Field/Option

Overview

Container path

Specify where you want to make the volume or bind mount available within the container's filesystem.

Mapping type

Select `Volume` to map a named volume, or select `Bind` to map a bind mount.

Volume

If using the `Volume` mapping type, select the named volume to mount from the dropdown.

Host path

If using the `Bind` mapping type, specify the path on the Docker host you want to bind mount in the container.

Writable / Read-only

Select `Writable` if you want the container to be able to write to the mapping. Select `Read-only` if the container should **not** be able to write to the mapping.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FuEb2dX7x25GHbRfTckqx%2F2.15-containers-advanced-volumes.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=52c1a349&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/advanced#network)

Network


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

In this section you can configure the network settings for the container.

Note that you cannot assign a static IP address to a container that is in Docker's default `bridge` network. This is a Docker limitation rather than Portainer. If you need to specify the IP for your container then you will need to [create a custom network](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/networks/add)
 and assign the container to it.

Field/Option

Overview

Network

Select the [network](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/networks)
 to attach the container to from the dropdown.

Hostname

Specify the hostname for the container.

Domain Name

Specify the domain name for the container.

Mac Address

Specify the MAC address to set on the container.

IPv4 Address

Specify the IPv4 address to use for the container. This must be within the range for the chosen network and should not be already assigned to a container.

IPv6 Address

Specify the IPv6 address to use for the container. This must be within the range for the chosen network and should not be already assigned to a container.

Primary DNS Server

Specify the primary DNS server to use within the container.

Secondary DNS Server

Specify the secondary DNS server to use within the container.

Hosts file entries

Click **add additional entry** to add a new host file entry for the container. Host file values should be formatted as `hostname:address` (for example `database:192.168.1.1`).

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2Fxjj37DEtKOCPqmKYkpIa%2F2.15-containers-advanced-network.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=bb11c6b5&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/advanced#env)

Env


--------------------------------------------------------------------------

Use this section to add or edit environment variables made available in the container. Click **Add an environment variable** to create a new variable, or edit an existing variable with the fields provided. You can also click **Load variables from .env file** to import an existing .env file with your variables. To remove a variable, click the trash can icon to the right of the variable to remove.

Field/Option

Overview

Name

Set the name for the environment variable.

Value

Set the value for the environment variable.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F2MjWbeHObNv2Juv0QEZz%2F2.15-containers-advanced-env.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b7646b7c&sv=2)

If you want to add multiple variables at once, click on **Advanced mode** to switch to an editor view where you can paste a block of variables and values.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/advanced#labels)

Labels


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can set labels on your container using this section. Click add label to add a new label, or edit an existing label using the fields provided. To remove a label, click the trash can icon to the right of the label to remove.

Field/Option

Overview

Name

Set the name for the label.

Value

Set the value for the label.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FwKmWk3PQoYqDY6W2dacW%2F2.15-containers-advanced-labels.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=f882b45c&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/advanced#restart-policy)

Restart policy


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Use this section to configure the restart policy for your container. Possible options are:

*   **Never**: Do not automatically restart the container when it exits. This is the default.
    
*   **Always**: Always restart the container regardless of the exit status. When you specify always, Docker will try to restart the container indefinitely. The container will also always start on Docker startup, regardless of the current state of the container.
    
*   **On failure**: Restart only if the container exits with a non-zero exit status.
    
*   **Unless stopped**: Always restart the container regardless of the exit status, including on Docker startup, except if the container was put into a stopped state before Docker was stopped.
    

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F4SSWez26sehlG1Qkhxmb%2F2.15-containers-advanced-restart.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=a226320&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/advanced#runtime-and-resources)

Runtime & Resources


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This section lets you configure runtime options for your container, add or configure GPUs for use within the container, and specify resource limitations on the container.

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/advanced#runtime)

Runtime

Here you can configure runtime options for the container.

Field/Option

Overview

Privileged mode

Enable this option to run the container in [privileged mode](https://docs.docker.com/engine/reference/run/#runtime-privilege-and-linux-capabilities)
.

Init

Enable this option to tell Docker that an init process should be used as PID 1 in the container.

Type

Select the runtime type to use to start the container. Options will depend on available runtimes on your Docker host.

Devices

Use this option to make devices on your Docker host available within the container. Click **add device** to add a new device, and define the **host** path for the device and the **container** path for where you want the device to appear within the container.

Sysctls

Use this option to specify sysctls to make available within the container. Click **add sysctl** to add a new sysctl, and set the **name** and **value** for your sysctl as required.

Shared memory size

Specify the size (in MB) of the shared memory device (`/dev/shm`) for the container.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FD3wUTCm9qOG8xwpWPyuZ%2F2.20-containers-advanced-runtime.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=37d51dab&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/advanced#gpu)

GPU

Here you can enable GPU access for the container and configure the GPU settings as required.

GPU support is currently only available on Docker Standalone environments, and only supports NVIDIA GPUs.

Field/Option

Overview

Enable GPU

Toggle this option on to enable GPU access for the container.

GPU selector

Select the GPU(s) to make available to the container, or choose `Use All GPUs` to provide access to all the GPUs on the Docker host.

Capabilities

Select the capabilities you want to use with the container. Portainer preselects `compute` and `utility` as they are the defaults when not specifying capabilities.

Control

View a generated equivalent of the Docker CLI's `--gpus` option based on your selections above.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FsK94ZibaNWk7Z0RKaDMG%2F2.20-containers-advanced-gpu.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=f94d46a2&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/advanced#resources)

Resources

Here you can configure resource limits for your container. You can use the sliders to set the value or enter a value in the fields.

Field/Option

Overview

Memory reservation (MB)

Specify the amount of memory (in MB) to reserve for the container.

Memory limit (MB)

Specify the maximum amount of memory (in MB) the container is allowed to use.

Maximum CPU usage

Specify the maximum amount of CPU the container is allowed to use. This is specified based on the number of processing threads available on your Docker host.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FaAmG3SsbiNeJ5eAenw2i%2F2.15-containers-advanced-resources.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=fc311112&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/advanced#capabilities)

Capabilities


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

In this section you can configure the individual capabilities for your container. For more information refer to the [Docker documentation](https://docs.docker.com/engine/reference/run/#runtime-privilege-and-linux-capabilities)
.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FVM2H7b3ZR0E9EWxcN0Xb%2F2.15-containers-advanced-capabilities.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=970e5676&sv=2)

[PreviousEdit or duplicate a container](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/edit)
[NextWebhooks](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/webhooks)

Was this helpful?

# Webhooks | Portainer Documentation

A webhook is a POST request sent to a URL that you define in Docker Hub or another registry. Use webhooks to trigger an action in response to an event such as a repository push.

This functionality is only available in [Portainer Business Edition](https://www.portainer.io/business-upsell?from=container-webhook)
.

Webhooks are only available on non-Edge environments (environments running Portainer Server or Portainer Agent, not the Portainer Edge Agent). This is because the tunnel to the Portainer Edge Agent is only opened on-demand, and therefore would mean there is no way to expose a webhook permanently.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/webhooks#enabling-a-container-webhook)

Enabling a container webhook


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

From the menu select **Containers** then select the container that you want to configure the webhook for.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F4eRl1DaLwHs4naEfin0e%2F2.15-docker_containers_container_details.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=4f5afbba&sv=2)

In the **Container details** screen toggle the **Container webhook** option on. When the URL appears, click **Copy link**. This URL will be used to configure the webhook in your chosen registry.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2Fl8F0bCDvh52oygXxFyZr%2F2.15-docker_containers_container_webhook.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=e8240a8d&sv=2)

This example shows how to trigger the webhook using `redeploy`:

Copy

    <form action="https://portainer:9443/api/webhooks/638e6967-ef77-4906-8af8-236800621360" method="post">
      Redeploy with latest image of same tag <input type="submit" />
    </form>

This example shows how to trigger the webhook to update the container to use a different image tag:

Copy

    <form action="https://portainer:9443/api/webhooks/638e6967-ef77-4906-8af8-236800621360?tag=latest" method="post">
      Update container image with different tag <input type="submit" />
    </form>

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/webhooks#configuring-the-webhook-in-docker-hub)

Configuring the webhook in Docker Hub


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To finish the configuration, refer to [Docker's own documentation](https://docs.docker.com/docker-hub/webhooks/)
.

[PreviousAdvanced container settings](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/advanced)
[NextAttach a volume to a container](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/attach-volume)

Was this helpful?

# View container logs | Portainer Documentation

From the menu select **Containers**, select the container then select **Logs**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FfOdx3hdqPkVGWsy7UHj1%2F2.30-containers-logs.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=e01b44a1&sv=2)

Here you can see the contents of the Docker logs for your container.

Field/Option

Overview

Search

Enter a string to search the log output. You can see the number of results for your search and move through each result with the up and down arrows.

Filter search results

When enabled, display only the log lines that contain your search string.

Copy

Click this button to copy the currently displayed log lines to your clipboard.

Download logs

Click this button to download your log.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FAm8KN2ZttjdHEtXERtob%2F2.17-containers-logs-search.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=2357374b&sv=2)

You can also set various options for how the logs are displayed:

Field/Option

Overview

Date picker

Select the time period from which to retrieve the logs.

Lines

Limit the number of lines per log file (the default is 1000).

Line numbers

When enabled, display line numbers for each log line.

Timestamp

When enabled, display a timestamp before each log line.

Wrap lines

When enabled, lines longer than the screen width will be wrapped onto the next line.

Auto refresh

Enable this option to automatically refresh the log view. When off, you can click the refresh icon to the right of the button to manually refresh the view.

Full screen

Click the full screen icon to expand the log display to fill your screen.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2Fx1Ol4rUsrClddAaNyRfo%2F2.30-containers-logs-options.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=170f3a9&sv=2)

[PreviousAttach a volume to a container](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/attach-volume)
[NextView container statistics](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/stats)

Was this helpful?

# Attach a volume to a container | Portainer Documentation

This article explains how to attach a new [volume](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/volumes)
 to a running container. This operation destroys the running container and starts a new one with the volume attached.

**Always back up your data before running this operation.**

From the menu select **Containers**, select the container that you want to attach a volume to, then click **Duplicate/Edit**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FqIMcLFfteYzLp0o52Gv8%2F2.15-docker_containers_container_edit.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=7792e7b6&sv=2)

Scroll down to **Advanced container settings**. Click **Volumes** then click **map additional volume**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FQlxu8pZL1XCInn90JZCi%2F2.15-docker_containers_container_add_volumes.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=27629005&sv=2)

In the **container** field enter the path. In the **volume** field enter the volume to attach to the container.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FinWu2Lncero8rnOyTxHa%2F2.15-docker_containers_container_adv_volume_mapping.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=d87049fc&sv=2)

When you're ready, click **Deploy the container**. When the confirmation message appears, click **Replace**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FbCMJmXKxKVtsTQ1R7BnJ%2F2.15-container-edit-confirm.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=50ef6dfe&sv=2)

[PreviousWebhooks](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/webhooks)
[NextView container logs](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/logs)

Was this helpful?

---

# View container statistics | Portainer Documentation

From the menu select **Containers**, select the container then select **Stats**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FKrhUVdpAPjirGCjnSYYn%2F2.15-docker_containers_container_stats.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=2dd85165&sv=2)

The information available includes:

*   Memory usage.
    
*   CPU usage.
    
*   Network usage (RX and TX).
    
*   I/O usage.
    
*   Processes running in the container
    

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FfcmbjatzT0HD3FDcSAfM%2F2.15-docker_containers_container_stats_usage.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=e99a680f&sv=2)

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F7N8rI65puTlwuemQMZ0f%2F2.15-docker_containers_container-stats-proc.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=176f54c0&sv=2)

You can change the refresh rate at any time.

[PreviousView container logs](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/logs)
[NextAccess a container's console](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/console)

# Remove a container | Portainer Documentation

From the menu select **Containers**, tick the checkbox next to the container you want to remove then click **Remove**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2Fw3WMAFjbcWTHT0T1MsmV%2F2.15-docker_containers_container_remove.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=8a23613e&sv=2)

When the confirmation message appears, opt whether or not to automatically remove non-persistent volumes then click **Remove**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FSqYUYXJHz52XGC7PdrLP%2F2.15-container-remove-confirm.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b27e2930&sv=2)

# Access a container's console | Portainer Documentation

From the menu select **Containers**, select the container then select **Console**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FuGkGgkSGJyWZVoEjrGR6%2F2.15-docker_containers_container_console.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=ec5122bd&sv=2)

Select the command and the user you want to give access to, then click **Connect**.

For Alpine Linux containers, you must select the`/bin/ash` command.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2Fz8qDsOaLgGvwTCL1D1Pf%2F2.15-docker_containers_container_console_execute.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=85bb8155&sv=2)

If you need to define a command other than those provided, toggle the **Use custom command** option on. Once connected, you can run commands in the console the same as any other Linux system.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FLghAMmqWXLgLu9p1pRJC%2F2.20-containers-console-connected.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=f5139961&sv=2)

To disconnect from the console session, click the **Disconnect** button.

[PreviousView container statistics](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/stats)
[NextChange container ownership](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/ownership)

Was this helpful?

# Import an image | Portainer Documentation

You can import images from other Portainer instances, the Docker CLI or the Docker Swarm CLI.

From the menu select **Images** then click **Import**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FplIlZZszkwqULC3FUdTt%2F2.15-docker_images_build_image_import.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=eaf72334&sv=2)

Click **Select file** to browse for the image file to upload. Portainer supports `.tar`, `.tar.gz`, `.tar.bz2` and `.tar.xz` files. If you are on a multi-node environment, select the node where you wish to save the image.

On a multi-node environment, the image you import will only be available on the node selected under **Deployment**. If you want to make the image available to all nodes, consider [adding a registry](https://docs.portainer.io/admin/registries/add)
 to Portainer.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FfmnFU4BsKzemMSmv2pkj%2F2.15-docker_images_upload_file.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=1b22c386&sv=2)

When importing an image you can also select to tag the image using a registry you have preconfigured in Portainer. Select the **Registry** from the dropdown and enter the image name and tag.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FLGKKm4gAOSJNH38rXKw3%2F2.15-docker_images_upload_file_tag_image.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=10df2bb9&sv=2)

If you wish to tag the image with a registry that is not configured within Portainer, click **Advanced mode** and enter the registry, port, image and tag as required.

If you want to tag the image locally rather than in a registry, use **Advanced mode** and simply specify the image name and tag, without a registry.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FzIchVi9Q9Koslr8dea2w%2F2.15-docker_images_import_simple.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b70b6dba&sv=2)

When you're ready, click **Upload** to import your image.

[PreviousBuild a new image](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/images/build)
[NextExport an image](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/images/export)

Last updated 2 months ago

Was this helpful?

# Images | Portainer Documentation

Images are what is used to build containers. Each image defines the pieces required to build and configure a container and can be reused many times. The **Images** section in Portainer lets you interact with the images in an environment.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FSJv17934JepPRWMoA8sN%2F2.15-images-splash.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=a42d5cd9&sv=2)

You can pull images from Docker Hub or any other [registry](https://docs.portainer.io/admin/registries/add)
:

[Pull an image](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/images/pull)

You can also view a list of the images that are currently available in an environment, including their IDs, usage states, tags, sizes and creation dates. There are many other options available:

[Build a new image](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/images/build)
[Import an image](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/images/import)
[Export an image](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/images/export)

[PreviousRemove a container](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/remove)
[NextPull an image](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/images/pull)

Was this helpful?

---

# Change container ownership | Portainer Documentation

Portainer allows you to limit container management to specific teams or users.

From the menu select **Containers** then select the container whose ownership you want to change.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F4eRl1DaLwHs4naEfin0e%2F2.15-docker_containers_container_details.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=4f5afbba&sv=2)

Under the **Access control** section tick the **Change ownership** checkbox then select the new ownership type, using the table below as a guide.

Ownership Type

Overview

Administrators

Only Portainer administrators can manage the container.

Restricted

Only teams or users you specify can manage the container.

Public

Anyone who has [access to the environment](https://docs.portainer.io/admin/environments/access)
 can manage the container.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F7wSdP4OU1JdjppLDT91Z%2F2.15-docker_containers_container_access_control.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=6a1edd30&sv=2)

When you've made your selection, click **Update ownership**. When the confirmation message appears, click **Change ownership**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FsQkXGCIxMyuPmhqOtuYj%2F2.15-container-ownership-confirm.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=f481d152&sv=2)

[PreviousAccess a container's console](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/console)
[NextRemove a container](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/remove)

Was this helpful?

---

# Pull an image | Portainer Documentation

You can pull images from any registry that has been [added to Portainer](https://docs.portainer.io/admin/registries)
, or using advanced mode, from a custom external registry.

On a multi-node environment, the pulled image will only be available on the node you select in the **Deployment** section. To make the image available to all nodes, consider [adding a registry](https://docs.portainer.io/admin/registries/add)
 to Portainer.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/images/pull#method-1-pulling-images-in-simple-mode)

Method 1: Pulling images in simple mode


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This method lets you pull images from Docker Hub or from another registry that you have connected with before.

From the menu select **Images**. Select the registry to use then enter the name of the image. On a multi-node environment, select the node to deploy to.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FnkmZOQM5BM6svKstBXdn%2F2.15-docker_images_pull_images.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=8205efbc&sv=2)

When you're ready, click **Pull the image**.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/images/pull#method-2-pulling-images-in-advanced-mode)

Method 2: Pulling images in advanced mode


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Using advanced mode, you can define a custom registry URL, port and image. This is ideal if you run your own private registry but don't want to add it to the [registries](https://docs.portainer.io/admin/registries)
 list in Portainer.

From the menu select **Images** then select **Advanced mode**. Next, enter the registry, port and image in the **Image** box. On a multi-node environment, select the node to deploy to.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FWtuFjlMjF4Z9lUXPSPJY%2F2.15-docker_images_pull_image_simple.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=72a4a8dd&sv=2)

When you're ready, click **Pull the image**.

[PreviousImages](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/images)
[NextBuild a new image](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/images/build)

Last updated 2 months ago

Was this helpful?

---

# Build a new image | Portainer Documentation

There are three ways you can build new images.

On a multi-node environment, the built image will only be available on the node you select in the **Deployment** section. To make the image available to all nodes, consider [adding a registry](https://docs.portainer.io/admin/registries/add)
 to Portainer.

When building an image with Portainer, you are unable to use `ADD` or `COPY` commands referencing files on the host. We recommend using `wget` or similar to retrieve files from a HTTP/S URL instead.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/images/build#method-1-using-the-portainer-web-editor)

Method 1: Using the Portainer web editor


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

From the menu select **Images** then click **Build a new image**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F2fyEwS6Pt3BxSNlBVW6s%2F2.15-docker_images_build_image.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=61ac69e1&sv=2)

Next, give the image a descriptive name (you can enter multiple names), select the **Web editor** option under **Build method**, then write your Dockerfile in the web editor.

You can search within the web editor at any time by pressing `Ctrl-F` (or `Cmd-F` on Mac).

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F39jma1ydo29EkDcg9xjK%2F2.15-docker_images_build_web_editor.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=53e7a215&sv=2)

Optionally, you can upload one or more local files to be included in an image by clicking **Select files** and selecting the files to include. You can then reference them in your Dockerfile.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FyjrnWetnHrteY5d0RdqQ%2F2.16-images-build-upload.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=c548c5e6&sv=2)

Select the node you want to save the image on (if on a multi-node environment) then click **Build the image**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FTj3xL0wSKbg63MiAY08o%2F2.15-docker_images_build_deployment.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=53e15f53&sv=2)

When the build is finished, select the **Output** tab to view the build history and the result.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/images/build#method-2-uploading-a-dockerfile)

Method 2: Uploading a Dockerfile


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If you have an existing Dockerfile, you can upload it to Portainer and use it to build the image.

From the menu select **Images** then click **Build a new image**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FEQuMbhKIfM9zhmTbDdlm%2F2.15-docker_images_build_image_upload.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=1125539d&sv=2)

Next, give the image a descriptive name (you can enter multiple names), select the **Upload** option under **Build method**, then browse to and upload the Dockerfile.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FS0QptvldEREJQARhfntH%2F2.15-docker_images_build_upload.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=2e9fe56a&sv=2)

Scroll down and select the node you want to save the image on (if on a multi-node environment) then click **Build the image**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FTj3xL0wSKbg63MiAY08o%2F2.15-docker_images_build_deployment.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=53e15f53&sv=2)

When the build is finished, select the **Output** tab to view the build history and the result.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/images/build#method-3-providing-a-dockerfile-from-a-url)

Method 3: Providing a Dockerfile from a URL


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If the Dockerfile is hosted on the Internet (either in a tarball or a public GitHub repository), you can download it directly to Portainer via its URL.

From the menu select **Images** then click **Build a new image**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FerdfAuCxZuG4KxGEpZOA%2F2.15-docker_images_build_image_URL.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=eb6c1b46&sv=2)

Next, give the image a descriptive name (you can enter multiple names), select the **Upload** option under **Build method**, then enter the **URL** of the file and the **Dockerfile path** within the tarball or repository.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FnsDi7MNmdSa8jfPJEJdl%2F2.15-docker_images_build_URL.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=4656af74&sv=2)

Scroll down and select the node you want to save the image on (if on a multi-node environment) click **Build the image**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FTj3xL0wSKbg63MiAY08o%2F2.15-docker_images_build_deployment.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=53e15f53&sv=2)

When the build is finished, select the **Output** tab to view the build history and the result.

[PreviousPull an image](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/images/pull)
[NextImport an image](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/images/import)

Last updated 2 months ago

Was this helpful?

---

# Export an image | Portainer Documentation

You can export any Docker image stored on any node. This is useful when you need to move a container from one host to another, or simply make a backup of the images.

If you export a container to a tar file, the volumes won't get exported with it. You will need to save the data from those volumes using a different method.

From the menu select **Images**, select the image you want to export then click **Export this image**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FyTwKJxCb41l1iV4TfuC8%2F2.15-docker_images_build_image_export.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=cfe560e1&sv=2)

When the warning message appears, click **Continue**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FocKKx3CvBWnt1mcSkWL1%2F2.15-images-export-confirm.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=5c4bff5c&sv=2)

When the image has downloaded, a success message will appear, and your browser should automatically download the resulting tar file.

[PreviousImport an image](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/images/import)
[NextNetworks](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/networks)

Last updated 2 months ago

Was this helpful?

---

# Remove a network | Portainer Documentation

You must detach all containers from a network before you can remove it.

From the menu select **Networks**, tick the checkbox next to the network you want to remove then click **Remove**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FxK25bdbZhy9GPs6zZPfJ%2F2.20-networks-remove.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=3d4b4391&sv=2)

To confirm the removal, click **Remove** in the dialog box.

[PreviousAdd a new network](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/networks/add)
[NextVolumes](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/volumes)

Was this helpful?

# Add a new network | Portainer Documentation

From the menu select **Networks** then click **Add network**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FHkFJce8cDi8kc9GpHsAD%2F2.20-networks-add.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=7c3419a9&sv=2)

Define the new network, using the table below as a guide.

Field/Option

Overview

Name

Give the network a descriptive name.

Driver

Define the [type of network](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/networks#supported-network-types)
 you will use.

Driver options

Set in place any options related to your network driver, if required.

IPv4 Network configuration

Define IPv4 range, subnet, gateway and exclude IP. If no information is entered here, Docker will automatically assign an IPv4 range. If you need to exclude IPs from the range, click **Add excluded IP** and complete the field.

IPv6 Network configuration

Define IPv6 range, subnet, gateway and exclude IP. If no information is entered here, Docker will automatically assign an IPv6 range. If you need to exclude IPs from the range, click **Add excluded IP** and complete the field.

Labels

Click **Add label** and complete the name and value fields to specify a label for the network.

Isolated network

Toggle this option on to isolate any containers created in this network to this network only, with no inbound or outbound connectivity.

Enable manual container attachment

Toggle this option on to allow users to attach the network to running containers.

Deployment

On multi-node clusters, select the node where the network will be created.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2Fdr4J5Gas0laufAoKg4TM%2F2.20-networks-add-details.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=c07849f&sv=2)

When you're finished, click **Create the network**.

[PreviousNetworks](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/networks)
[NextRemove a network](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/networks/remove)

Last updated 2 months ago

# Networks | Portainer Documentation

Portainer lets you add, remove and manage networks in your environment.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FvyzCjc3ynGWTuRj3aWuC%2F2.20-networks-list.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=95062efd&sv=2)

[Add a new network](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/networks/add)
[Remove a network](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/networks/remove)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/networks#supported-network-types)

Supported network types


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Portainer supports these types of networks:

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/networks#bridge)

bridge

If you don’t specify a driver, this type of network will be created by default. Bridge networks are normally used when your applications run in standalone containers that need to communicate with each other.

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/networks#macvlan)

macvlan

macvlan networks allow you to assign a MAC address to a container, making it appear as a physical device on your network. The Docker daemon routes traffic to containers based on their MAC addresses. Using the macvlan driver is sometimes the best choice when dealing with legacy applications that expect to be directly connected to the physical network, rather than routed through the Docker host’s network stack.

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/networks#ipvlan)

ipvlan

Similar to macvlan, the key difference being that the endpoints have the same MAC address. ipvlan supports L2 and L3 modes. In ipvlan L2 mode, each endpoint gets the same MAC address but different IP addresses. In ipvlan L3 mode, packets are routed between endpoints, giving better scalability.

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/networks#overlay)

overlay

overlay networks connect multiple Docker daemons together and enable swarm services to communicate with each other. You can also use overlay networks to facilitate communication between a swarm service and a standalone container, or between two standalone containers on different Docker daemons.

[PreviousExport an image](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/images/export)
[NextAdd a new network](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/networks/add)

Last updated 2 months ago

Was this helpful?

---

# Volumes | Portainer Documentation

A volume is a data storage area that can be mounted into a container to provide persistent storage. Unlike bind mounts, volumes are independent of the underlying OS and are fully managed by the Docker Engine.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F709gjWPxhPXG3FS8uB6U%2F2.15-docker_volumes_volumes.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=1a597bbd&sv=2)

A volume with the **external** flag was created outside of Portainer, which means Portainer has limited knowledge on it compared to one created within Portainer. A label of **unused** means that Portainer cannot see any applications that are using this volume. This label may also appear on **external** resources because of the limited information available.

In Portainer you can view a list of the volumes on your environment, add new volumes and remove existing volumes.

[Add a new volume](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/volumes/add)
[Remove a volume](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/volumes/remove)

If you're running Docker Swarm or the Portainer Agent on your environment, you can also browse existing volumes on that environment.

[Browse a volume](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/volumes/browse)

[PreviousRemove a network](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/networks/remove)
[NextAdd a new volume](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/volumes/add)

Was this helpful?

---

# Browse a volume | Portainer Documentation

This feature is only available when running Docker Swarm or the Portainer Agent on the environment.

From the menu select **Volumes** then click **browse** next to the volume you want to explore.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F2GHDNq1PdpuydWoRirNt%2F2.15-docker_volumes_volume_browse.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=adf89bcf&sv=2)

You can upload files to the volume (by clicking the icon in the top right), and quickly expose them to the container without the need for a CLI. You can also download, rename and delete files in the volume.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F3yLSLDHxzMu1faHIzte8%2F2.15-docker_volumes_volume_browser_files.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=deb59ca9&sv=2)

Adding a tmpfs volume


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

From the menu select **Volumes** then click **Add volume**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F45M8DJFQ0z7z5OyHBImi%2F2.15-docker_volumes_add_volume.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=67863044&sv=2)

Overview

Name

Give the volume a descriptive name.

Driver

Select `local`.

*   name: `type`

*   name: `device`
    
    value: `tmpfs`
    
*   name: `o`

Toggle this off.

Use CIFS volume

Toggle this off.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FpBoJG26UsRJE3aphjHjn%2F2.15-docker_volumes_volume_console_exec_tmpfs.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=60d95c7f&sv=2)

# Configs | Portainer Documentation

The **Configs** menu is only available to Docker Swarm environments.

Docker 17.06 introduced swarm service configs which allow you to store non-sensitive information, such as configuration files, outside a service’s image or running containers. This allows you to keep your images as generic as possible, without the need to bind-mount configuration files into the containers or use environment variables. [Secrets](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/secrets)
 is another option for storing sensitive information.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FpTm5zYfUUTfL7LVhx3l5%2F2.15-docker_configs_config_list.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=2dae0b18&sv=2)

In Portainer you can add and remove custom configurations for use in deployments.

[Add a new config](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/configs/add)
[Remove a config](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/configs/remove)

[PreviousRemove a volume](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/volumes/remove)
[NextAdd a new config](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/configs/add)

Was this helpful?

---

# Secrets | Portainer Documentation

The Secrets menu is only available to Docker Swarm environments.

A secret is a blob of data, such as a password, SSH private key, SSL certificate, or another piece of data that should not be transmitted over a network, stored unencrypted in a Dockerfile, or stored in your application’s source code. In Docker 1.13 and later, you can use Docker Secrets to centrally manage this data and securely transmit it only to those containers that need access to it.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FIyyHyUFab9AHjdIXQsh6%2F2.15-docker_secrets_secrets_list.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9ed60458&sv=2)

Secrets are encrypted during transit and at rest in Docker Swarm. A given secret is only accessible to those services which have been granted explicit access to it, and only while those service tasks are running.

You can use secrets to manage any sensitive data that a container needs at runtime, but you don’t want to store in the image or in source control, such as:

*   Usernames and passwords.
    
*   TLS certificates and keys.
    
*   SSH keys.
    
*   Other important data such as the name of a database or internal server.
    
*   Generic strings or binary content (up to 500Kb in size).
    

For less sensitive data or larger content, see [configs](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/configs)
.

In Portainer you can add and remove secrets for use in deployments.

[Add a new secret](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/secrets/add)
[Remove a secret](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/secrets/remove)

[PreviousRemove a config](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/configs/remove)
[NextAdd a new secret](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/secrets/add)

Was this helpful?

---

# Details | Portainer Documentation

This page provides information about the Docker host for the selected environment. The page is split into the following sections: Host Details, Engine Details, and (if enabled) PCI Devices and Physical Disks.

This page is only available on Docker Standalone environments.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/host/details#host-details)

Host Details


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This section describes the host's basic configuration, including the hostname, OS information, kernel version, total CPU and memory. If the environment has the Portainer Agent installed, [host management features](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/host/setup#enable-host-management-features)
 are enabled, and a `/host` mount has been configured, you can also browse the host file system from here.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2Fzge9epay0fcKYJjGUSVN%2F2.15-docker-host-details.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=621c81a6&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/host/details#engine-details)

Engine Details


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Learn more about the Docker or Podman engine running on your environment, including the Docker/Podman version, the root directory, storage and logging drivers and available volume and network plugins.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FEdEwioQj6tclAHJrCi5b%2F2.15-docker-host-engine.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=c2812473&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/host/details#pci-devices-and-physical-disks)

PCI Devices and Physical Disks


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

These sections list the available PCI devices and physical disks on the host.

These sections are only visible when [host management features](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/host/setup#enable-host-management-features)
 are enabled for the environment.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2Fxai4ZAjmcGJjPk3HSAYK%2F2.15-docker-host-pci.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=fc2261ac&sv=2)

# Setup | Portainer Documentation

The **Host Setup** section is only available to Docker Standalone environments.

Under **Setup**, you can make changes to your environment, enabling and disabling features and security settings.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/host/setup#host-and-filesystem)

Host and Filesystem


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

For environments running the Portainer Agent, this section is where you configure how Portainer interacts with elements of the host.

For security, these features are disabled by default. Be sure that you understand their impact before enabling them.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FlBy2RWDakuCPXo86Kn94%2F2.22.0-host-setup-filesystem.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=e283610d&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/host/setup#enable-host-management-features)

Enable host management features

Enabling host management features allows you to see the available devices and storage on the physical node as well as browse the node's filesystem. The environment must be [running the Portainer Agent](https://docs.portainer.io/start/agent)
 to use this functionality, and the root of the host must be bind-mounted to`/host` in the agent deployment:

Copy

    -v /:/host

For example, starting the Portainer Agent on Docker on Linux with the host filesystem mounted at `/host`:

Copy

    docker run -d -p 9001:9001 --name portainer_agent --restart=always -v /var/run/docker.sock:/var/run/docker.sock -v /var/lib/docker/volumes:/var/lib/docker/volumes -v /:/host portainer/agent:2.22.0

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/host/setup#enable-volume-management-for-non-administrators)

Enable volume management for non-administrators

Enabling this feature allows non-administrator users to manage volumes on an environment. If this is disabled, users below administrator level have read-only access to volumes.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/host/setup#change-window-settings)

Change Window Settings


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This setting allows you to specify a window within which [GitOps updates](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/stacks/add#gitops-updates)
 to your applications can be applied.

If this setting is enabled and an update is made to an application outside of this window, it will not be applied.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FvMphMTnryG7VmViSVHT8%2F2.19-kubernetes-cluster-setup-changewindow.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=83282b8&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/host/setup#docker-security-settings)

Docker Security Settings


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This section allows you to toggle assorted Docker-related security settings for the environment.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FEgpquYgLdZSFygG6iwWu%2F2.15-docker_hosts_security_settings.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=67b3d699&sv=2)

Option

Overview

Disable bind mounts for non-administrators

Prevents non-admin users within Portainer from using bind mounts when creating containers and/or services/stacks. When toggled on, the option to attach to a host file system path is removed.

Disable privileged mode for non-administrators

Prevents non-admin users from elevating the privilege of a container to bypass SELinux/AppArmor. When toggled on, the option to select **Privileged** mode when [adding a container](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/add)
 is removed.

Disable the use of host PID 1 for non-administrators

Prevents non-admin users from requesting that a deployed container operates as the host PID. This is a security risk if used by a non-trustworthy authorized user because when they operate as PID1, they are in effect able to run any command in the container console as root on the host.

Disable the use of Stacks for non-administrators

This is a 'sledgehammer' approach to removing any possibility for non-admin users within Portainer to find and use weaknesses in the Docker architecture. Whilst Portainer has the ability to disable some of the more common exploits, we cannot possibly block them all because there are any number of capabilities that could be added to a container to attempt to gain access to the host. This feature simply allows an admin to disable all possible entry points.

Disable device mappings for non-administrators

Blocks users from mapping host devices into containers. Whilst the ability to map devices is generally used for good (e.g. mapping a GPU into a container), it can equally be used by non-trustworthy authorized users to map a physical storage device into a container. It is possible to mount `/dev/sda1` into a container, and then from a console of that container, the user would have complete access to the sda1 device without restriction. By toggling this on, Portainer blocks the ability for non-admins to map ANY devices into containers.

Disable container capabilities for non-administrators

Toggle on to hide the **Container capabilities** tab for non-administrators when they are [adding a container](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/add)
.

Disable sysctl settings for non-administrators

Toggle on to stop non-admin users from using sysctl options, preventing them from recreating, duplicating or editing containers.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/host/setup#other)

Other


---------------------------------------------------------------------

This section contains other assorted environment-specific settings.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2Fr8DcPqZ7CQpOcvpfU9E9%2F2.18-host-setup-other.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b9cb2285&sv=2)

Option

Overview

Show GPU in the UI

Toggle on to enable GPU assignments in the Portainer UI. This adds additional processing to the container and stack listing pages, so if you are not using GPUs on your environment we recommend toggling this off.

Add GPU

When **Show GPU in the UI** is toggled on, click Add GPU to add GPUs to your environment for use by your containers. To add a GPU, provide a name for the GPU and an index or UUID to reference the GPU.

Show an image(s) up to date indicator for Stacks, Services and Containers

Toggle on to enable the [new image indicator](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers)
 feature for this environment. Toggle off to disable the feature. This feature is only available in Portainer Business Edition.

[PreviousDetails](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/host/details)
[NextRegistries](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/host/registries)

Was this helpful?

---

# Registries | Portainer Documentation

**Registries** lets you manage access to each of the registries that are currently available.

Registry access assigned here only applies to the selected environment. It is not global.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/host/registries#adding-a-new-registry)

Adding a new registry


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

From the menu select **Host**, select **Registries** then click **Add registry**. When the global registries page appears, follow [these instructions](https://docs.portainer.io/admin/registries/add)
.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FIgmVH6JpWddL4V33Hx4T%2F2.15-host-registries-add.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=4530512d&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/host/registries#managing-access)

Managing access


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To configure access to a registry, from the menu select **Host** then select **Registries**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FuUoTmHtIrNDYVSuHehx4%2F2.15-docker_hosts_registries.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=5c5b490&sv=2)

Find the registry you want to manage then select **Manage access**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F1wh1ydVTdLcF8EWHTGJe%2F2.15-docker_hosts_registries_manage_access.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=97340692&sv=2)

From the dropdown, select the users or teams that you would like to have access, then click **Create access**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FMVmOuD2bykRy3lVgkdq4%2F2.15-docker_hosts_registries_access.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=57c1b25a&sv=2)

[PreviousSetup](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/host/setup)
[NextSwarm](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/swarm)

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/swarm/cluster-visualizer#options)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/swarm/cluster-visualizer#refresh)

Use this option to define the refresh rate of the visualizer (the default is every 5 seconds).

# Details | Portainer Documentation

This page provides information about the Docker Swarm cluster for the selected environment. The page is split into the following sections: Cluster status and Nodes, with clicking a node name taking you to the Node overview for that node.

This page is only available on Docker Swarm environments.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/swarm/details#cluster-status)

Cluster status


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This section describes the cluster's basic configuration, including the number of nodes, the Docker API version, and the total CPU and memory available. A link to the [cluster visualizer](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/swarm/cluster-visualizer)
 is also included.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F3lXVXZIZBsMacdVncvpq%2F2.15-swarm-clusterstatus.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=3c77b895&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/swarm/details#nodes)

Nodes


------------------------------------------------------------------------

Lists all of the nodes in the cluster along with a summary of each node, including:

*   The role of the node.
    
*   The number of CPUs and memory available on the node.
    
*   The Docker Engine version running on the node.
    
*   The node's IP address.
    
*   The status and availability of the node.
    

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FD8zwInMciT6k4k60gB8i%2F2.15-swarm-nodes.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=4f9ce2c5&sv=2)

Clicking on an individual node's name will take you to an overview page for that node.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/swarm/details#node-overview)

Node overview


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/swarm/details#host-details)

Host Details

This section describes the node's basic configuration, including the hostname, OS information, and total CPU and memory.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FnVash4VUKhRFEnX1ATuG%2F2.15-swarm-nodedetail.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=eaf31d09&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/swarm/details#engine-details)

Engine Details

Information such as the Docker version and the available volume and network plugins helps you to understand more about the Docker engine running on your node.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FAdTqze120PFimqVOST9M%2F2.15-swarm-nodedetail-engine.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=22dfdf72&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/swarm/details#pci-devices-and-physical-disks)

PCI Devices and Physical Disks

These sections list the available PCI devices and physical disks on the node.

These sections are only visible when [host management features](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/swarm/setup#host-and-filesystem)
 are enabled for the cluster.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2Fxai4ZAjmcGJjPk3HSAYK%2F2.15-docker-host-pci.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=fc2261ac&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/swarm/details#node-details)

Node Details

Here you'll find details about the node's configuration as part of the cluster. You can view the role, set the availability status of the node, view the current status and apply labels to the node.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FAQK2dDFTeniMIFyLxrTW%2F2.15-swarm-nodedetail-detail.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=1d680a63&sv=2)

Host and Filesystem


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This section is where you configure how Portainer interacts with elements of the host.

For security, these features are disabled by default. Be sure that you understand their impact before enabling them.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FnIguGK3WbcRGDttE6Ln3%2F2.15-docker_hosts_features_config.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=61f2c400&sv=2)

Option

Overview

Enable host management features

Enabling host management features allows you to see the available devices and storage on the physical nodes across your cluster as well as browse the nodes' filesystems.

Enable volume management for non-administrators

Enabling this feature allows non-administrator users to manage volumes on an environment. If this is disabled, users below administrator level have read-only access to volumes.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/swarm/setup#change-window-settings)

Change Window Settings


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This setting allows you to specify a window within which [GitOps updates](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/stacks/add#gitops-updates)
 to your applications can be applied.

If this setting is enabled and an update is made to an application outside of this window, it will not be applied.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FvMphMTnryG7VmViSVHT8%2F2.19-kubernetes-cluster-setup-changewindow.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=83282b8&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/swarm/setup#docker-security-settings)

Docker Security Settings


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This section allows you to toggle assorted Docker-related security settings for an environment.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FEgpquYgLdZSFygG6iwWu%2F2.15-docker_hosts_security_settings.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=67b3d699&sv=2)

Option

Overview

Disable bind mounts for non-administrators

Prevents non-admin users within Portainer from using bind mounts when creating containers and/or services/stacks. When toggled on, the option to attach to a host file system path is removed.

Disable privileged mode for non-administrators

Prevents non-admin users from elevating the privilege of a container to bypass SELinux/AppArmor. When toggled on, the option to select **Privileged** mode when [adding a container](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/add)

Disable the use of host PID 1 for non-administrators

Prevents non-admin users from requesting that a deployed container operates as the host PID. This is a security risk if used by a non-trustworthy authorized user because when they operate as PID1, they are in effect able to run any command in the container console as root on the host.

Disable the use of Stacks for non-administrators

This is a 'sledgehammer' approach to removing any possibility for non-admin users within Portainer to find and use weaknesses in the Docker architecture. Whilst Portainer has the ability to disable some of the more common exploits, we cannot possibly block them all because there are any number of capabilities that could be added to a container to attempt to gain access to the host. This feature simply allows an admin to disable all possible entry points.

Blocks users from mapping host devices into containers. Toggle on to hide the **Container capabilities** tab for non-administrators when they are [adding a container](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/containers/add)
.

Disable sysctl settings for non-administrators

Toggle on to stop non-admin users from using sysctl options, preventing them from recreating, duplicating or editing containers.

# Registries | Portainer Documentation

**Registries** lets you manage access to each of the registries that are currently available.

Registry access assigned here only applies to the selected environment. It is not global.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/docker/swarm/registries#adding-a-new-registry)

Adding a new registry


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

From the menu select **Swarm**, select **Registries** then click **Add registry**. When the global registries page appears, follow [these instructions](https://docs.portainer.io/admin/registries/add)
.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FGJDMlpN0gqA2gAb7SURZ%2F2.15-docker_swarm_add_registries.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=45474ac4&sv=2)

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FVQU7VGTpOa55nSKEPJaX%2F2.15-docker_swarm_registries_manage_access.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=37232113&sv=2)

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FgvTf87YhTlZp339q1A1r%2F2.15-docker_swarm_registry_manage_access.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=7d2f318c&sv=2)

From the dropdown, select the users or teams that you would like to have access then click **Create access**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FMVmOuD2bykRy3lVgkdq4%2F2.15-docker_hosts_registries_access.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=57c1b25a&sv=2)

# Dashboard | Portainer Documentation

The Kubernetes dashboard summarizes your Kubernetes environment and shows the components that make up the environment.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/dashboard#environment-info)

Environment info


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This section shows the environment name, its URL and port, along with any [tags](https://docs.portainer.io/admin/environments/tags#tagging-an-environment)
.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FXGQDJiRZ3wdYg5JD6S4y%2F2.15-kubernetes_env_info.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=1d86124b&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/dashboard#summary-tiles)

Summary tiles


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

, [applications](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications)
, [services](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/networking/services)
, [ingresses](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/networking/ingresses)
, ConfigMaps, secrets, and [volumes](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/volumes)
 that make up the environment.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F9Fve85ixf7rHFRwaO0I6%2F2.19-kubernetes-dashboard-tiles.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b9d8e746&sv=2)

# kubectl shell | Portainer Documentation

Although the Portainer UI provides access to a lot of Kubernetes functionality, sometimes you need to drop into the console. We have provided a shell within the UI that includes `kubectl` and `helm` binaries. The shell is preloaded with a `kubeconfig` for the user's context, restricting access to the permissions defined in Portainer for that user.

To access the shell, select **kubectl shell** from the menu. Once the shell loads, you can run `kubectl` and `helm` commands as needed.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3850702872-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%252Fuploads%252FN0IGzgPjD6w3jqdqzVdT%252F2.33-kube-shell.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D195d18a3-21e3-4de7-ade4-849d91594749&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=85e240f5&sv=2)

[PreviousDashboard](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/dashboard)
[NextKubeconfig](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/kubeconfig)

Last updated 2 months ago

Was this helpful?
