# Add a new custom template | Portainer Documentation

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/templates/add#creating-the-template)

Creating the template


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

From the menu select **Custom Templates** then click **Add Custom Template**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FheiKOR6SuozChnyz3dqa%2F2.19-kubernetes-templates-add.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=75bb7f2b&sv=2)

Complete the form, using the table below as a guide.

Field/Option

Overview

Title

Enter a title for your custom template. This is how the template will appear when it's deployed.

Description

Enter a description of the template.

Note

As an optional step, record some extra information about the template.

Icon URL

Optionally, enter the URL to an image to use as an icon for the template.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F4V63HVRLQfWiRBKDpnnK%2F2.15-kubernetes_create_custom_template.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=53d22046&sv=2)

Next, select the **Build method**.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/templates/add#selecting-the-build-method)

Selecting the build method


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/templates/add#method-1-web-editor)

Method 1: Web editor

Define or paste the contents of your manifest file into the web editor. When deploying an application using a custom template you will be given an opportunity to edit the manifest before deployment.

You can search within the web editor at any time by pressing `Ctrl-F` (or `Cmd-F` on Mac).

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FYQZoFCa0W9xyKzWgGrGk%2F2.19-kubernetes-templates-add-web.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=30462077&sv=2)

When you're ready, click **Create custom template**.

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/templates/add#method-2-upload)

Method 2: Upload

If you have a manifest file locally, you can upload it directly to Portainer. Click **Select file** to browse to the file.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FlmYDBGnuE6Sr7Tbo2twN%2F2.19-kubernetes-templates-add-upload.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=c985b3a1&sv=2)

When you're ready, click **Create custom template**.

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/templates/add#method-3-repository)

Method 3: Repository

If you have a template in a Git repository, you can add it to your custom templates. Enter the required details for access to your Git repository.

Field/Option

Overview

Authentication

Toggle this option on if your repository requires authentication.

Git credentials

If you have credentials configured you can select the set to use from this dropdown.

Username

Enter your Git username.

Personal access token

Enter your personal access token or password.

Repository URL

Enter the URL to your Git repository.

Repository reference

Select the reference to use from your repository. This will be auto populated with available references from your repository.

Manifest path

Enter the path and filename of the manifest within your repository.

Skip TLS Verification

Toggle this option on to skip TLS verification for the repository. This is useful if you are using self-signed certificates on your repo.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2Fe4RYsn4HDRNRvPLl2yse%2F2.19-kubernetes-templates-add-git.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=62154105&sv=2)

When you're ready, click **Create custom template**.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/templates/add#variables-in-templates)

Variables in templates


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Custom templates support the use of variables to provide further customization of the deployed stack. A stack can define a variable that can then be adjusted by the user at deployment.

This feature is only available in Portainer Business Edition.

Variables are identified in stacks with `{{ }}`. For example, the following stack provides a `REPLICA_COUNT` variable:

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2Fu0Y7bH7YtqN4fHcBLctd%2F2.19-kubernetes-templates-add-variables.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=66b46142&sv=2)

When a variable is defined, options appear to customize how the variable appears when deploying the stack. You can set the **label**, **description** and **default value**.

When a template is deployed, any variables that have been configured are editable:

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FLtosIX4UsAqAtjpNlrdl%2F2.19-kubernetes-templates-add-variables-deploy.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=c40f4c42&sv=2)

[PreviousCustom Templates](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/templates)
[NextEdit a custom template](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/templates/edit)

Last updated 2 months ago

Was this helpful?

# Custom Templates | Portainer Documentation

Portainer BE 2.10 added custom template support for Kubernetes environments, allowing you to create templates based on Kubernetes manifests for future deployment.

From the menu select **Custom Templates** to view a list of custom templates you've already created.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FNOTCLnQc15NYJzyFStcM%2F2.15-k8s_kubernetes_custom_templates.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=184fb9c5&sv=2)

You can create a new template.

[Add a new custom template](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/templates/add)

You can also edit an existing template.

[Edit a custom template](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/templates/edit)

And, if you no longer need a custom template, you can simply remove it.

[Remove a custom template](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/templates/remove)

# Namespaces | Portainer Documentation

Namespaces used to be called 'resource pools' prior to Portainer CE 2.6.0.

In Kubernetes, a single physical cluster can support multiple virtual clusters. These are known as namespaces.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FhcVIs85EciVpKLYJoCBv%2F2.24.0-kubernetes-namespaces-list.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=eefa2865&sv=2)

You can add, remove or manage namespaces in Portainer.

[Add a new namespace](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/add)
[Manage a namespace](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/manage)
[Manage access to a namespace](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/access)
[Remove a namespace](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/remove)

[PreviousRemove a custom template](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/templates/remove)
[NextAdd a new namespace](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/add)

Was this helpful?

---

# Kubeconfig | Portainer Documentation

Portainer can act as a proxy for other Kubernetes management tools, providing access to the Kubernetes cluster while still retaining the security and governance that Portainer provides. A user can download their own `kubeconfig` file and use it with their favorite tool to access the Kubernetes cluster with only the permissions afforded to that user. To generate and download your `kubeconfig` file, from the Home page click the **kubeconfig** button.

You must be accessing Portainer via HTTPS for the kubeconfig button to appear. If you are logged in with HTTP, you will not see the option.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2Fn5UZwxBVm2M6hfymnvnX%2F2.15-k8s-kubeconfig.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=2f2cfa68&sv=2)

You will be asked to select the Kubernetes environments that you would like in your `kubeconfig` file. If you have configured a [kubeconfig expiry](https://docs.portainer.io/admin/settings#kubeconfig-expiry)
 value, this will also be shown.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FPNCqvt9AjLCm2QrNbxUK%2F2.15-k8s-kubeconfig-confirm.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=7b0baea4&sv=2)

Tick the boxes for the environments you need and click **Download File**.

A downloaded `kubeconfig` file will look something like the example below.

Note that the server URL is set to the Portainer Server instance, not the Kubernetes cluster.

Copy

    apiVersion: v1
    clusters:
    - cluster:
        insecure-skip-tls-verify: true
        server: https://my-portainer-server:9443/api/endpoints/1/kubernetes
      name: portainer-cluster-kubernetes
    contexts:
    - context:
        cluster: portainer-cluster-kubernetes
        user: portainer-sa-clusteradmin
      name: portainer-ctx-kubernetes
    current-context: portainer-ctx-kubernetes
    kind: Config
    preferences: {}
    users:
    - name: portainer-sa-clusteradmin
      user:
        token: xxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxx

Each environment in the `kubeconfig` will be accessible via contexts. Access is set based on the specific user that created the `kubeconfig` file.

Unless set to never expire, tokens will expire after the defined period, at which point a new `kubeconfig` file will need to be generated. An administrator can [adjust the token expiry behavior](https://docs.portainer.io/admin/settings#kubeconfig-expiry)
 on the **Settings** page.

Adjusting the token expiry will not affect previously generated `kubeconfig` files.

[Previouskubectl shell](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/kubectl)
[NextCustom Templates](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/templates)

Last updated 2 months ago

Was this helpful?

# Edit a custom template | Portainer Documentation

From the menu select **Custom Templates** then click **Edit** next to the template you want to edit.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FLe71BJ3DuTcaBWAqDNxt%2F2.15-k8s_kubernetes_edit_custom_templates.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=ba417d87&sv=2)

You can search within the web editor at any time by pressing `Ctrl-F` (or `Cmd-F` on Mac).

If your template is deployed from a Git repository, you will have the option to edit the Git settings if required. You can also click **Reload custom template** to update the template from the remote repository.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FTsRQfDVfo6rTkRmGZSJr%2F2.19-kubernetes-templates-edit-git.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9278c0e1&sv=2)

Make the required changes to the template then click **Update the template**.

[PreviousAdd a new custom template](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/templates/add)
[NextRemove a custom template](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/templates/remove)

# Remove a custom template | Portainer Documentation

Removing a custom template will not remove any deployments created using the template.

From the menu select **Custom Templates** then click **Delete** next to the template you want to remove.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F6Swkf4w5Zejn5nL3ux7m%2F2.15-k8s_kubernetes_delete_custom_templates.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=a400f151&sv=2)

When the confirmation message appears, click **Remove**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FAGEXHQHCGGipD3ALwa2I%2F2.15-k8s-templates-remove-confirm.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=19486cc9&sv=2)

[NextNamespaces](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces)

# Add a new namespace | Portainer Documentation

From the menu select **Namespaces** then click **Add with form**.

Namespaces can also be added [using a manifest](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/manifest)
 by clicking **Create from manifest**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FzPi9kUo3UJ38rDZlcoSV%2F2.20-namespaces-add.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=773fdaec&sv=2)

Give the namespace a descriptive **name**. As an optional step you can add annotations to your namespace as required by clicking **Add annotation** and filling in the **Key** and **Value** fields.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F3W0eWiwGAmy8CppTo1JP%2F2.18-k8s-namespaces-add-name.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=ffbdfedb&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/add#resource-quota)

Resource quota

You can assign a quota by toggling **Resource assignment** on, then setting resource limits like how much memory and CPU will be assigned.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FGp8l3GBg64TUVwf2DJga%2F2.20-kubernetes-namespaces-add-resourcequota.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=45e3c68c&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/add#load-balancers)

Load balancers

To set a maximum number of external load balancers that can be created inside the namespace, toggle on **Load Balancer quota** and set the **Max Load Balancers** number. If Load Balancer quota is enabled and the Max Load Balancers value is set to `0`, the use of external load balancers is effectively disabled in the namespace.

This section is only visible when **Allow users to use external load balancers** is enabled in the [Cluster Setup](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/cluster/setup#allow-users-to-use-external-load-balancer)
.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FAuovJT0YB7l6rGjcY5QH%2F2.18-k8s-namespaces-add-lbquota.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=67fc5eaf&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/add#networking-ingresses)

Networking - Ingresses

This section lets you define which ingress controllers are allowed to be used to publish applications within this namespace. Check the boxes next to the ingresses you want to allow and click **Allow selected**, or click **Disallow selected** to disallow their use in this namespace.

This section is only visible when **Configure ingress controller availability per namespace** is enabled in the [Cluster Setup](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/cluster/setup#networking-ingresses)
.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FUv8hfRq92R7f2BIZmvUq%2F2.20-namespaces-add-ingress.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9e58a604&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/add#registries)

Registries

You can define the registries that are available within this namespace in this section. Select the registries from the **Select registries** dropdown to allow access.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FMN9sz8XQT98pJNbLYXxW%2F2.18-k8s-namespaces-add-registries.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=518dfb69&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/add#storage)

Storage

Use this section to enable quotas on your storage options for this namespace. To enable the use of quotas on a storage option, toggle **Enable quota** to on and set the **Maximum usage**. A Maximum usage value of `0` effectively prevents the usage of that storage option within the namespace.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FKy1lLG7U6wer31S0bHSc%2F2.18-k8s-namespaces-add-storage.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=991e870b&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/add#summary)

Summary

This section displays a summary of the actions that will be taken when clicking the Add namespace button.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2Fd5a8VRGZHPTelqQZbU29%2F2.18-k8s-namespaces-add-summary.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=bc818371&sv=2)

When you're finished, click **Create namespace**.

[PreviousNamespaces](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces)
[NextManage a namespace](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/manage)

Was this helpful?

---

# Remove a namespace | Portainer Documentation

From the menu select **Namespaces**, tick the checkbox next to the namespace then click **Remove**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FEriFO2xWzRjQzTQfxE7Z%2F2.20-namespaces-remove.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=a93c1656&sv=2)

When the confirmation message appears, click **Remove**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FfIWlERVU4kgY7C8sE1TY%2F2.15-k8s-namespaces-remove-confirm.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=1df36fac&sv=2)

If a namespace is stuck in a terminating state, Portainer will ask if you want to force deletion of that namespace.

[PreviousManage access to a namespace](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/access)
[NextApplications](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications)

Last updated 2 months ago

# Manage a namespace | Portainer Documentation

From the menu select **Namespaces** then select the namespace you want to manage.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FkiXHRS3zJR8iA3ZLqDQz%2F2.20-namespaces-manage.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=c47ef1b0&sv=2)

Here you can view details about the namespace and configure options specific to the namespace.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/manage#resource-quota)

Resource Quota


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Toggle on **Resource assignment** to enable quotas for this namespace, then define the memory and CPU limits. The current resource reservation and usage for the namespace will be displayed when a limit is set.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F6AQvQtC72ccNTVTLcYxE%2F2.25-kubernetes-namespaces-manage-resourcequota.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=bcea854f&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/manage#load-balancers)

Load balancers


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

With this setting you can configure the amount of external load balancers that can be created in this namespace.

This option only appears when **Allow users to use external load balancer** is enabled in the [cluster setup](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/cluster/setup#allow-users-to-use-external-load-balancer)
.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FDhyJ8mAZ2xEymR2GhMXc%2F2.17-k8s-namespaces-manage-loadbalancer.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=c9728ce1&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/manage#networking)

Networking


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This section lets you define which ingress controllers are allowed to be used to publish applications within this namespace. Check the boxes next to the ingresses you want to allow and click **Allow selected**, or click **Disallow selected** to disallow their use in this namespace.

This section is only visible when **Configure ingress controller availability per namespace** is enabled in the [Cluster Setup](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/cluster/setup#networking-ingresses)
.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FUv8hfRq92R7f2BIZmvUq%2F2.20-namespaces-add-ingress.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9e58a604&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/manage#registries)

Registries


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can define the registries that are available within this namespace in this section. Select the registries from the **Select registries** dropdown to allow access.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FMN9sz8XQT98pJNbLYXxW%2F2.18-k8s-namespaces-add-registries.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=518dfb69&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/manage#storage)

Storage


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

For each storage option available in the cluster, you can configure quotas for this namespace to limit usage.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F0mb9BHhC3AbLqTBYJbyf%2F2.15-kubernetes_namespaces_manage_namespace_storage.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=2a28796f&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/manage#summary)

Summary


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If you have made changes to the configuration, this section will list those changes.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2Fa0EVUFh8kIRsp8XoHZR4%2F2.15-kubernetes_namespaces_manage_namespaces_summary.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=5be3547a&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/manage#actions)

Actions


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Once you have made the necessary changes, click **Update namespace**. Here you can also flag the namespace as a system namespace by clicking **Mark as system**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FW7iGdlzKzGDZ9INzCSAR%2F2.15-kubernetes_namespaces_manage_namespaces_actions.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=4efaba67&sv=2)

[PreviousAdd a new namespace](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/add)
[NextManage access to a namespace](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/access)

Was this helpful?

# Manage access to a namespace | Portainer Documentation

Kubernetes role-based access control (RBAC) must be enabled and working before access control will work in Portainer.

From the menu select **Namespaces** then select **Manage access** on the same row as the namespace you want to manage.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FO4giPUFdQ4PjA7BQ14nR%2F2.20-namespaces-access.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=4c1965f3&sv=2)

Select the users/teams who will have access then click **Create access**.

Users or groups with cluster-wide roles (such as the Operator role) cannot be assigned to individual namespaces, as their cluster-wide nature applies to all namespaces in the environment.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FgXRju8jPcwsqBD5EjQfP%2F2.20-namespaces-access-create.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=2aa63569&sv=2)

[PreviousManage a namespace](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/manage)
[NextRemove a namespace](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/remove)

Last updated 2 months ago

Was this helpful?

# Applications | Portainer Documentation

In Kubernetes, an application is a collection of configuration settings and variables required to run your app. This may consist of a single container or multiple containers with complex interoperability.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FTqtwOGjNYWTQrpqy8C4P%2F2.27-kubernetes-applications-list.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=3283c23c&sv=2)

You can filter the list of applications by namespace using the **Namespace** dropdown.

Portainer lets you add applications either using a form or through code (for example a manifest or a Helm chart):

[Add a new application using a form](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/add)
[Add a new application using code](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/manifest)

You can also inspect a running application:

[Inspect an application](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect)
[Inspect a Helm application](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect-helm)

Applications can be edited, webhooks can be configured and volumes can be detached:

[Edit an application](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/edit)
[Webhooks](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/webhooks)
[Detach a volume from an application](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/detach-volume)

If you no longer require an application, it can be removed:

[Remove an application](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/remove)

[PreviousRemove a namespace](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/namespaces/remove)
[NextAdd a new application using a form](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/add)

Was this helpful?

# Add a new application using a form | Portainer Documentation

There are two ways to add a new application: manually by using a form, or automatically by [using code](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/manifest)
. This article explains how to add an application using a form.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FuKZG9pK8ywMwSwOvrSvH%2F2.24.0-kubernetes-applications-form-add.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=74188263&sv=2)

Complete the required information, using the sections below as a guide.

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/add#base-configuration)

Base configuration

Field/Option

Overview

Namespace

Select the namespace where the application will reside.

Name

Give the application a descriptive name.

Registry

Select the registry to pull the image from. If you want to pull from a registry that is not configured with Portainer, click **Advanced mode** then enter the URL and image manually.

Image

Enter the name (and optionally the tag) of the image that will be used to deploy the application.

Note

Enter a note to provide additional details about the application. This field is mandatory if the [Require a note on applications](https://docs.portainer.io/admin/settings#deployment-options)
 toggle is enabled in Settings.

Annotations

You can add annotations to your application as required by clicking **Add annotation** and filling in the **Key** and **Value** fields.

Stack

Portainer can automatically bundle multiple applications inside a stack. You can either enter the name of a new stack, select an existing stack from the list, or leave empty to use the application name.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FAprAeB9aFjsKkAKYxqf2%2F2.20-kubernetes-applications-add-base.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=f2b5fa06&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/add#environment-variables)

Environment variables

Here you can define any environment variables you wish to be available to your application.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FOxg3ZVZqBGOsNGfUOnNO%2F2.18-k8s-applications-add-envvar.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=14dbbbc1&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/add#configmaps)

ConfigMaps

Select any ConfigMaps you have previously created to make them available to the application. Portainer will automatically expose all the keys of a ConfigMap as environment variables. This behavior can be overridden to filesystem mounts for each key via the **Override** button.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FQGct1M9MBAO1vbKbP4y0%2F2.19-kubernetes-applications-add-form-configmaps.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=3a21aa91&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/add#secrets)

Secrets

Select any secrets you have previously created to make them available to the application. Portainer will automatically expose all the keys of a secret as environment variables. This behavior can be overridden to filesystem mounts for each key via the **Override** button.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2Fit3q78UMZQPVRWYKChWZ%2F2.19-kubernetes-applications-add-form-secrets.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=97fdc2b1&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/add#persisted-folders)

Persisted folders

Define any persistent folders within the application and whether these are new or existing volumes, as well as the size of the volume and storage location.

You can also define the **Data access policy** for your persisted folders:

*   **Isolated:** Each instance of the application will use its own data.
    
*   **Shared**: All application instances will use the same data.
    

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FEzaIlGpxAy60T2Lhzu7R%2F2.18-k8s-applications-add-persisted.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=31ee0235&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/add#resource-reservations)

Resource reservations

In this section you can define the amount of memory and CPU requested by the application as well as the upper limits for memory and CPU that the application is permitted to use. If the namespace you have selected has resource quotas set, you must define at least the request values.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3850702872-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%252Fuploads%252FPAZABtUQ6KX762JQib9J%252F2.33-kubernetes-applications-form-resource-reservations.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd93e5b15-b14c-456c-8e54-385bf1ce7ce5&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=7af5562f&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/add#deployment)

Deployment

This section allows you to choose how you want to deploy the application inside the cluster. Options are:

*   **Replicated:** Run one or multiple instances of this container.
    
*   **Global:** Deploy an instance of this container on each cluster node.
    

You can also define the number of instances of the application to run by setting the **Instance count**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FYlnhwq62AOQUCXCHCOVr%2F2.15-kubernetes_applications_add_form_deployment.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=2c5d507e&sv=2)

Toggle **Enable auto scaling for this application** to enable auto-scaling for the application you are deploying. This requires that the Kubernetes metrics server is installed and [enabled in the cluster setup](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/cluster/setup#resources-and-metrics)
.

Field/Option

Overview

Minimum instances

Enter the minimum number of instances that you want running for this application.

Maximum instances

Enter the maximum number of instances that you want running for this application.

Target CPU usage

Enter the target CPU percentage for your application. The autoscaler will ensure that enough instances are running to maintain an average CPU usage of this value across all instances.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FA11HjYkx5W7E7t6P6lxn%2F2.20-kubernetes-applications-add-autoscaling.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=1834d62b&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/add#placement-preferences-and-constraints)

Placement preferences and constraints

Here you can define which placement rules must be followed by the nodes where the application is deployed to. Placement rules are based on node labels. To create a new rule, click **add rule**.

You can also define the placement policy for the rules you have set. Options are:

*   **Mandatory:** The application will only be scheduled on nodes that follow all rules.
    
*   **Preferred**: If possible, the application will be scheduled on nodes that follow all rules.
    

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FFrUtwE4SjJIlWZlfRGzX%2F2.20-kubernetes-applications-add-placementprefs.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=80775dc5&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/add#publishing-the-application)

Publishing the application

Here you can create the necessary services to expose your application. Select the type of service (ClusterIP, NodePort, or LoadBalancer) from the tabs and click **Create service**. You can then configure each service as required, including adding annotations to the services if required.

You can expand the **Explanation** link for more detail on how each service type works.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FlJUnxAHfYgfDmnufPu2l%2F2.19-kubernetes-applications-add-publishing.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=6d18dd27&sv=2)

When you have finished, click **Deploy application**.

[PreviousApplications](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications)
[NextAdd a new application using code](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/manifest)

# Detach a volume from an application | Portainer Documentation

From the menu select **Applications**, select the application then click **Edit this application**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F65BcauSiLmKV8vjAGgLf%2F2.20-kubernetes-applications-edit.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=e362e4b7&sv=2)

Scroll down to the **Persisting data** section and click the trash can icon to the right of the volume. Scroll down and click **Update application**. When the confirmation message appears, click **Update**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FFH9YTGXgbeNfJDdKRF70%2F2.15-k8s-applications-detach-confirm.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=5068eed4&sv=2)

# Webhooks | Portainer Documentation

A webhook is a POST request sent to a URL. Use webhooks to trigger an action in response to an event such as a repository push.

This functionality is only available in [Portainer Business Edition](https://www.portainer.io/business-upsell?from=stack-webhook)
.

Webhooks are only available on non-Edge environments (environments running Portainer Server or Portainer Agent, not the Portainer Edge Agent). This is because the tunnel to the Portainer Edge Agent is only opened on-demand, and therefore would mean there is no way to expose a webhook permanently.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/webhooks#enabling-an-application-webhook)

Enabling an application webhook


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

From the menu select **Applications** then select the application that you want to configure the webhook for. Then select the **Edit this application** button.

Webhooks are only available for applications deployed from a Git repository.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2Fr5pwoUdU7U3cHhLsV7XT%2F2.20-kubernetes-applications-webhooks.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=4fbfbb5b&sv=2)

Enable **GitOps updates** if it is not already enabled and select `Webhook` as the **Mechanism**. When the URL appears, click **Copy link**. This is the URL used to trigger the webhook.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FpfWZ02fcPak8S4xob9lD%2F2.19-kubernetes-applications-webhooks-git.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=20272869&sv=2)

This example shows how to trigger the webhook:

Copy

    <form action="https://portainer:9443/api/stacks/webhooks/40ac1662-47c3-4a8e-b148-2a34eb52bb42" method="post">
      Redeploy application <input type="submit" />
    </form>

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/webhooks#using-environment-variables-with-webhooks)

Using environment variables with webhooks


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

When triggering a webhook, environment variables can be passed through the endpoint and referenced within the deployment.

Environment variables can not be updated for Pods, only for Deployments.

To specify an environment variable on a webhook, add it as a variable to the URL. For example, to pass a `SERVICE_TAG` variable with the value `development`:

Copy

    https://portainer:9443/api/stacks/webhooks/40ac1662-47c3-4a8e-b148-2a34eb52bb42?SERVICE_TAG=development

To reference the `SERVICE_TAG` variable in your manifest with a fallback to the value `stable`:

Copy

    apiVersion: apps/v1
    kind: Deployment
    metadata:
      name: nginx-deployment
    spec:
      selector:
        matchLabels:
          app: nginx
      replicas: 2
      template:
        metadata:
          labels:
            app: nginx
        spec:
          containers:
          - name: nginx
            image: nginx:1.14.2
            ports:
            - containerPort: 80
            env:
            - name: SERVICE_TAG 
              value: "stable"

Environment variables must already be defined in the manifest - new environment variables cannot be added via the webhook.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/webhooks#rolling-restarts)

Rolling restarts


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

When using an application's webhook to redeploy your application, you can tell Portainer to perform a rolling restart of the application rather than a "terminate and restart" redeploy.

This functionality is only available in Portainer Business Edition.

To specify this, use the `rollout-restart` parameter in your webhook call:

Copy

    https://portainer:9443/api/stacks/webhooks/40ac1662-47c3-4a8e-b148-2a34eb52bb42?rollout-restart=all

Valid options are as below:

Option

Overview

`rollout-restart=all`

All of the application's deployments will be redeployed as a rolling restart.

`rollout-restart=deployment/deployment1,deployment/deployment2`

Only the specified deployment(s) will be redeployed as a rolling restart. All other deployments will not be redeployed or restarted. Separate multiple deployments with commas. This option supports Deployments (`deployment/deployment1`), DaemonSets (`daemonset/daemonset1`), and StatefulSets (`statefulset/statefulset1`).

If the `rollout-restart` parameter is not defined, the webhook will redeploy the application in traditional "terminate and restart" behavior.

If your cluster has a [change window](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/cluster/setup#change-window-settings)
 enabled, the rolling restart will only be performed within the change window.

[PreviousEdit an application](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/edit)
[NextDetach a volume from an application](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/detach-volume)

Was this helpful?

---

# Edit an application | Portainer Documentation

From the menu select **Applications**, select the application you want to edit, then click **Edit this application**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F65BcauSiLmKV8vjAGgLf%2F2.20-kubernetes-applications-edit.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=e362e4b7&sv=2)

Your editing options will depend on how the application was deployed initially.

Regardless of the deployment method, you can [edit an application's YAML directly](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect#yaml-tab)
 through the YAML tab in Portainer Business Edition.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/edit#applications-deployed-from-git)

Applications deployed from Git


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If the application was [deployed from a Git repository](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/manifest#repository)
 you can redeploy it from the repository if needed. You will see the repository URL that the application was deployed from, the current version deployed, and the file used for the deployment.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2Fh48EI93714IkwdZXpGVy%2F2.19-kubernetes-applications-edit-git-info.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=80a4b8fe&sv=2)

You can reconfigure GitOps updates, the repository reference and authentication here if needed. If a change window is enabled, information on it will appear here as well.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FcnBkvAnGbAeLGxhz9uIB%2F2.20-kubernetes-applications-edit-gitops.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9c0a367c&sv=2)

If you want to redeploy, click **Pull and update application**. If you're simply updating the repository settings and don't need to redeploy, click **Save settings**.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/edit#applications-deployed-from-the-web-editor)

Applications deployed from the Web Editor


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If the application was deployed from the Web Editor, you will be given the ability to edit the manifest manually.

You can search within the web editor at any time by pressing `Ctrl-F` (or `Cmd-F` on Mac).

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FqAZV0nFQy0AD208Yubc4%2F2.20-kubernetes-applications-edit-webeditor.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=67502349&sv=2)

Make the required changes then click **Update application**.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/edit#applications-deployed-from-a-form-or-helm)

Applications deployed from a form or Helm


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

When editing an application deployed from a form or Helm, you will be able to update the configuration using the same form. Refer to [adding a new application using a form](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/add)
 for details.

[PreviousInspect a Helm application](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect-helm)
[NextWebhooks](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/webhooks)

Was this helpful?

---

# Inspect an application | Portainer Documentation

To view information about applications running in a cluster, from the menu select **Applications** then select the application you want to inspect.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FKAqti0IEebjDh22uhgvK%2F2.20-kubernetes-applications-inspect.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=f05e62c8&sv=2)

The **Application details** screen is organized into four sections. The following tables explain all of the information to be found in each.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect#application-tab)

Application tab


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Attribute

Overview

Name

The name of the application.

Stack

The stack that the application belongs to (if any).

Namespace

The namespace that the application is running in.

Application Type

The type of application (Pod, Deployment, StatefulSet, DaemonSet, etc).

Status

Indicates whether or not the application is running. Where applicable, this also shows the replication state and number of replicas.

Creation

Shows when the application was created and by whom, as well as how the application was deployed.

Note

Add a note about the application or edit an existing note.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FwlOC3fLfQO9fWp0Ji81q%2F2.20-kubernetes-applications-inspect-application.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=741d2107&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect#placement-tab)

Placement tab


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Here you'll find information about any placement constraints or preferences that have been defined for the application and how they're being applied.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FXUWDqpzWSRsUgmMG7XBa%2F2.20-kubernetes-applications-inspect-placement.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=346be122&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect#events-tab)

Events tab


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Shows information about application-related events.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FxO0KwMgjM09uoDJuIpHZ%2F2.20-kubernetes-applications-inspect-events.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=3631655c&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect#yaml-tab)

YAML tab


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This displays the YAML generated from the application deployment, and lets you edit the YAML for an application directly. Updates to your manifest made here are applied using the Kubernetes `patch` mechanism.

Editing your YAML through this section is only available in Portainer Business Edition.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FKMCR34aNBItBTpAmV157%2F2.20-kubernetes-applications-inspect-yaml.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b56db0d8&sv=2)

Make your edits then click **Apply changes** to update the deployment.

Editing the YAML is not available for resources in namespaces marked as system.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect#actions)

Actions


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Depending on how the application was deployed, a number of actions can be performed, including:

*   [Editing the application](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/edit)
    .
    
*   Perform a rolling restart of the application (Business Edition only).
    
*   Redeploying the application (terminating all the services and recreating them).
    
*   Rolling the application back to a previous configuration.
    
*   Creating a [template](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/templates)
     from the application.
    

When using a Git repository, the rolling restart and redeploy options do not re-pull the manifest from the upstream repository. To do this, use the **Pull and update application** button when [editing an application](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/edit#method-1-redeploy-from-git)
.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FuVKeXwdmz8gYafAsYr5d%2F2.17-k8s-applications-inspect-actions.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=dbc001a3&sv=2)

Some of the potential actions that may appear for your application

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect#configuration-details)

Configuration details

Configuration

Overview

Accessing the application

Shows which ports (if any) are published from the container.

Auto-scaling

Indicates the application's auto-scaling policy.

Environment variables, ConfigMaps or Secrets

A list of any environment variables, ConfigMaps and secrets that have been defined for the application.

Data persistence

A list of the persistent folders and their details.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2Fo73vGCUb3uCVbYmrxImn%2F2.20-kubernetes-applications-inspect-configdetails.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=bc11b3ab&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect#application-containers)

Application containers


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

See which pods run your application, which image is being used, the status, node, and IP address of the pod, and when each pod was created. You can also access the pod stats, console and logs from here.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FxyEfnXmoIZ6HzIvX96jA%2F2.20-kubernetes-applications-inspect-appcontainers.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=7226625d&sv=2)

[PreviousAdd a new application using code](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/manifest)
[NextInspect a Helm application](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect-helm)

# Add a new application using code | Portainer Documentation

There are two ways to add a new application: [manually by using a form](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/add)
 or automatically by using code. This article explains how to add an application using code.

Creating from code isn't just for applications - you can also deploy namespaces, ingresses, ConfigMaps, secrets, volumes and more using code.

First, from the left hand menu select **Applications** then click **Create from code**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2Flo1DaI8TKFM4QA64NgbD%2F2.24.0-kubernetes-applications-manifest-add.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=cdf0b606&sv=2)

Next, select your deployment method from the **Deploy from** section.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FVgvElI7MzpSW9CWSMiGn%2F2.20-kubernetes-applications-manifest-deployfrom.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=56e4d000&sv=2)

Then, select the namespace to deploy to and optionally provide a stack name for your deployment in the **Deploy to** section.

If you want to use namespaces defined in your manifest, you can leave **Namespace** set to `default` and toggle on the **Use namespace(s) specified from manifest** option. This option is not available for deployments from Helm charts.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FbFnupbbbgAuyL8sHgUZt%2F2.20-kubernetes-applications-manifest-namespace.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=5da1ccca&sv=2)

Your next options will depend on the deployment method you selected.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/manifest#web-editor)

Web editor


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Use the Web editor to write or paste in your Kubernetes manifest.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FBTzmNDO1u26xNrucLCyp%2F2.20-kubernetes-applications-manifest-webeditor.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=ea472546&sv=2)

You can search within the web editor at any time by pressing `Ctrl-F` (or `Cmd-F` on Mac).

When you're ready, click **Deploy**.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/manifest#url)

URL


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Enter the **URL** to your manifest file in the provided field.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FvhmWUXECk1BbogDFVXK2%2F2.20-kubernetes-applications-manifest-url.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=d24f6084&sv=2)

When you're ready, click **Deploy**.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/manifest#repository)

Repository


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Use the provided fields to enter the details of your Git repository containing your Kubernetes manifests.

When an application is deployed from Git, Portainer will clone the entire Git repository as part of the deployment process. Ensure you have enough free space to accommodate this.

Portainer's Git deployment functionality does not currently support the use of Git submodules. If your repository includes submodules, they will not be pulled as part of the deployment. We [hope to add support](https://github.com/orgs/portainer/discussions/9767)
 for submodules in a future release.

Field/Option

Overview

Authentication

Toggle this on if your repository requires authentication.

Git Credentials

If the **Authentication** toggle is enabled and you have [configured Git credentials](https://docs.portainer.io/user/account-settings#git-credentials)
, you can select them from this dropdown.

Authorization type

Select either **Basic** or **Token** authorization depending on what your Git repository requires. For example, GitHub uses Basic authorization and Bitbucket uses Token authorization.

Username

Enter your Git username.

Personal Access Token

Enter your personal access token or password.

Save credential

Check this option to save the credentials entered above for future use under the name provided in the **credential name** field.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3850702872-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%252Fuploads%252FzmfqJr9riBkwBDLbvERB%252F2.33-stacks-add-git-authentication.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Db5c64ef1-bece-407b-8416-e9d4b5a8f7b0&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=806dfd13&sv=2)

Field/Option

Overview

Repository URL

Enter the repository URL. If you have enabled Authentication above the credentials will be used to access the repository. The below options will be populated by what is found in the repository.

Skip TLS Verification

Toggle this on to skip the verification of TLS certificates used by your repository. This is useful if your repo uses a self-signed certificate.

Repository reference

Select the reference to use when deploying the stack (for example, the branch).

Manifest path

Enter the path to your manifest file relative to the root of your repository.

Additional paths

Click **Add file** to define additional manifests or compose files to process as part of the deployment.

GitOps updates

Toggle this on to enable GitOps updates (see below).

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FEqkTTXzeOJux538PPapk%2F2.24.0-kubernetes-applications-manifest-git.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9c62131f&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/manifest#gitops-updates)

GitOps updates

Enabling GitOps updates gives Portainer the ability to update your application automatically, either by polling the repository at a defined interval for changes or by using a webhook to trigger an update.

For more detail on how GitOps updates function under the hood, have a look at [this knowledge base article](https://portal.portainer.io/knowledge/how-do-automatic-updates-for-stacks-applications-work)
.

If your application is configured for GitOps updates and you make changes locally, these changes will be overridden by the application definition in the Git repository. Bear this in mind when making configuration changes.

Field/Option

Overview

Mechanism

Choose from **Polling** or **Webhook**.

Fetch interval

When using the **Polling** method, choose how often you wish to check the Git repository for updates to your application.

Webhook

When using the **Webhook** method, this displays the webhook URL to use. Click **Copy link** to copy the webhook to your clipboard. For more on webhooks, refer to the [webhook documentation](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/webhooks)
.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FhqxDAuyM5wJ9wbUuveNP%2F2.19-stacks-add-git-polling.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=6eefc0bc&sv=2)

GitOps updates using the polling mechanism

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FBoH1Wtn65fBv1gK2zJbK%2F2.19-stacks-add-git-webhook.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=8e22805a&sv=2)

GitOps updates using the webhook mechanism

Field/Option

Overview

Always apply manifest

Enable this setting to force the redeployment of your application (kubectl apply) at the specified interval (or when the webhook is triggered), overwriting any changes that have been made in the local environment, even if there has been no update to the application in Git. This is useful if you want to ensure that your Git repository is the source of truth for your applications and are happy with the local application being replaced.

If this option is left disabled, automatic updates will only trigger if Portainer detects a change in the remote Git repository.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FXcWlkSp53pdUbJUgiF2S%2F2.19-kubernetes-ingress-add-manifest-git-alwaysapply.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=8a92cec2&sv=2)

When you're ready, click **Deploy**.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/manifest#custom-template)

Custom template


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

From the **Template** dropdown, select the custom template to use. Depending on the template, you may need (or be able) to set template variables that will adjust the deployment configuration. As an optional step, you can edit the template before deploying the application. If you have no custom templates you will be given a link to the [Custom Templates](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/templates)
 section.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FwzmrsQQxkRsrDiEfR737%2F2.20-kubernetes-applications-manifest-customtemplate.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b5e8be5c&sv=2)

When you're ready, click **Deploy**.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/manifest#helm-chart)

Helm chart


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Once you have selected a namespace for your Helm deployment you will need to specify a **Name** for your deployment. Next, select a **Helm chart source** to pull charts from in the dropdown. Portainer will then pull the chart list from the selected registry and display them below. Select a chart to use from the list provided. You can search within the list and filter by category.

Business Edition users will be able to choose charts from OCI registries if they have been [configured](https://docs.portainer.io/admin/registries)
 and [given access to the selected namespace](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/cluster/registries#managing-access)
.

When a Helm chart source is chosen for the first time, it may take some time to download and populate the charts in the list.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FT5gJW4y9ZwogX8VBMa00%2F2.32-kubernetes-applications-deploy-helm-deployto.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=6fb14509&sv=2)

Once you have selected a chart, Portainer will import the `values.yaml` file for the latest version of the chart and display it in the right hand pane as a reference. You can make any necessary customizations to the `values.yaml` file in the left-hand pane. You can also choose to deploy a different version of the chart by choosing the version from the **Version** dropdown.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FhilnFdgPeC8QkhH3e1IK%2F2.32-kubernetes-applications-deploy-helm-values.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=48789b7c&sv=2)

Once you've made your customizations, you can begin the deployment by clicking **Install**.

[PreviousAdd a new application using a form](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/add)
[NextInspect an application](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect)

# Remove an application | Portainer Documentation

From the menu select **Applications**, tick the checkbox next to the application you want to remove then click **Remove**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FC6xfUgFPoWTdZohpWSM4%2F2.20-kubernetes-applications-remove.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=ad680b39&sv=2)

When the confirmation message appears, click **Remove**.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F5sDxzkQWrxYMQ1uKOF4f%2F2.15-k8s-applications-remove-confirm.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=d7b05a&sv=2)

[PreviousDetach a volume from an application](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/detach-volume)
[NextNetworking](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/networking)

# Services | Portainer Documentation

In Kubernetes, a **Service** is an object that is used to expose an application (running in pods) to a network.

The Services page lists the services within your cluster, and provides detail on each service. To view the list of services, expand **Networking** and select **Services** from the left hand menu.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FBsz5JUolGilYFknN4wRS%2F2.20-kubernetes-networking-services.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=128789db&sv=2)

All the services the user has access to are listed on this page.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F6g5SWWXC4JaxSGJhcE0I%2F2.20-kubernetes-networking-services-list.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=a177103&sv=2)

For each service, the list displays the **name** of the service, the **application** and **namespace** the service belongs to, the **type** of service, the exposed **ports** and **target ports**, the **cluster IP** and **external IP** (if any) and the **creation date** and **user** (if available). Services provisioned externally to Portainer are marked with the **external** label, and system services are marked with the **system** label.

The display of system services can be toggled under the table settings (click the three dots at the top right of the table and tick **Show system resources**.

[PreviousNetworking](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/networking)
[NextIngresses](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/networking/ingresses)

Was this helpful?

---

# Inspect a Helm application | Portainer Documentation

To view information about Helm applications running in a cluster, from the menu select **Applications** then select the Helm application you want to inspect.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FbPEObBF5fHCTb3gQZpTb%2F2.29-kubernetes-applications-inspect-helm.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=34356e45&sv=2)

You will be shown details about the Helm application including the name, namespace, revision, chart used for the deployment, the chart source, the application version, the chart version, and the last deployment date. You'll also find buttons to [edit or upgrade](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect-helm#upgrading)
, roll back or uninstall your Helm deployment.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FTttu6gyfgY9lyrfyyi45%2F2.32-kubernetes-applications-helm-details-header.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=6132b204&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect-helm#revisions)

Revisions


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

On the right side of the page you will also see a list of revisions for your Helm deployment.

On smaller displays the revisions list is hidden by default - click the View revisions link to display them.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FOQyIqxTpzaC1zKlorc2E%2F2.30-kubernetes-helm-revisions-list.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=fd38558c&sv=2)

Revisions can be used to roll back your deployment to a previous state if something goes wrong. To rollback to a specific revision, select the revision from the sidebar and then click the **Rollback** button.

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect-helm#editing-or-upgrading)

Editing or Upgrading


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

With Helm chart versioning, a Helm deployment can be upgraded or downgraded through Portainer. If a newer version of your currently deployed chart is available, a new version notification will be displayed on under the Upgrade button. You can click the **Refresh** link to update the list of versions from the chart source.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FbQKII4JBkvHguBfYRxDn%2F2.32-kubernetes-applications-helm-details-buttons.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=af189323&sv=2)

To make changes to, upgrade, or downgrade a Helm deployment, click on the **Edit/Upgrade** button. In the resulting popup, choose the chart version to switch to (your current version will be labeled) and make any adjustments to the values. The default values for the version you have chosen is displayed on the right as a read-only reference. You can also choose whether to **Rollback on failure** by checking the box.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F8R88dipHOMojthwUir28%2F2.32-kubernetes-applications-helm-details-upgrade.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=cbe9b9e9&sv=2)

When you're ready, click **Edit/Upgrade**. The upgrade will begin and you will be returned to the details page for the application.

The status of the upgrade will be displayed on the details page and you can check the **Events** tab for details.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2F39dkZFUdY4wT6a5m8S3R%2F2.32-kubernetes-applications-helm-details-upgrading.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9692f044&sv=2)

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect-helm#deployment-details)

Deployment details


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You will also see five tabs that provide additional information about your Helm deployment: [Resources](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect-helm#resources)
, [Events](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect-helm#events)
, [Values](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect-helm#values)
, [Manifest](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect-helm#manifest)
 and [Notes](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect-helm#notes)
.

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect-helm#resources)

Resources

The **Resources** tab displays information about the resources that make up your Helm deployment. The items listed here will vary depending on the contents of your Helm chart. The **Name**, **Resource type**, **Status**, **Status message** and **Actions** are shown for each resource.

Only resources currently in the cluster will be displayed on this tab.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2Fwbwi144pTEbE9KNSlQ9v%2F2.30-kubernetes-helm-details-resources.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9ceab5c4&sv=2)

Click on the name of select resource types (such as Deployments and Pods) to [view details of that specific resource](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect)
. Clicking the **Describe** link for a resource will display a raw description of the resource in a popup window.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FuWCL5HmQ2DAgFT2R7sLd%2F2.29-kubernetes-applications-inspect-helm-resource-describe.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=e634e286&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect-helm#events)

Events

The **Events** tab lists the events related to the deployment of this application. Events listed here are relative to the events TTL setting on the underlying Kubernetes environment, so will disappear after some time.

Only events for resources currently in the cluster will be displayed on this tab.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2Fdb3t7FYFGCz5dCr6K5VL%2F2.30-kubernetes-helm-details-events.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=fba65e7c&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect-helm#values)

Values

The **Values** tab shows the raw values set on the deployment. By default the **View** option is selected which shows the currently deployed values, but choosing **Diff with previous** or **Diff with specific revision** (and specifying a revision) lets you compare the currently deployed values with those of a previous revision. You can check the **User defined only** option to display only those options explicitly specified by the chart, or untick it to show all values including globally set options.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FY1EZpLOFdVcK0i5Xvbx2%2F2.30-kubernetes-helm-details-values.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=7f8e8710&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect-helm#manifest)

Manifest

The **Manifest** tab displays the raw manifest used to deploy the Helm chart. By default the **View** option is selected which shows the currently deployed manifest, but choosing **Diff with previous** or **Diff with specific revision** (and specifying a revision) lets you compare the currently deployed manifest with that of a previous revision.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2Fv474nEg0hJ6Sb73jDbJf%2F2.30-kubernetes-helm-details-manifest.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=d0d34abb&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect-helm#notes)

Notes

The **Notes** tab displays any notes that were attached to the Helm chart when it was deployed. By default the **View** option is selected which shows the currently deployed notes, but choosing **Diff with previous** or **Diff with specific revision** (and specifying a revision) lets you compare the currently deployed notes with those of a previous revision.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FtftmElAVVsWCxEXZgGHl%2F2.30-kubernetes-helm-details-notes.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=84a78d3c&sv=2)

[PreviousInspect an application](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/inspect)
[NextEdit an application](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/applications/edit)

Was this helpful?

# Ingresses | Portainer Documentation

An **Ingress** in Kubernetes is an API object that provides routing rules to manage external users' access to the services in a Kubernetes cluster, typically via HTTPS/HTTP. With Ingress, you can easily set up rules for routing traffic without creating a bunch of Load Balancers or exposing each service on the node.

To view, edit or create ingresses in your environment, expand **Networking** and select **Ingresses** from the left hand menu.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FQt96cNw2VsikPudtlXoL%2F2.20-kubernetes-networking-ingresses.gif&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=bd969999&sv=2)

All the Ingresses that a user has access to are listed on this page.

![](https://docs.portainer.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FXI7douejaBgpZ6CP2zJf%2Fblobs%2FF9K3HiMleOHMqzXWJfQY%2F2.20-kubernetes-networking-ingresses-list.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=69dc470a&sv=2)

New Ingress objects can be created either manually or through a manifest:

[Add an Ingress manually](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/networking/ingresses/add)
[Add an Ingress using a manifest](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/networking/ingresses/manifest)

If you no longer require an Ingress, it can be removed:

[Remove an Ingress](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/networking/ingresses/remove-an-ingress)

[PreviousServices](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/networking/services)
[NextAdd an Ingress manually](https://docs.portainer.io/user/kubernetes/networking/ingresses/add)

Was this helpful?
